  • Ice berg (openberg) deterministic
  • View page source

Click here to download the full example code

Ice berg (openberg) deterministic

from opendrift.readers import reader_netCDF_CF_generic
from opendrift.models.openberg import OpenBerg

Initialize model

steps = 60  # This is the number of forecast steps

o = OpenBerg()  # Basic drift model suitable for icebergs

Out:

13:03:37 DEBUG   opendrift.models.basemodel: Adding 17 config items from basemodel
13:03:37 DEBUG   opendrift.models.basemodel: Adding 5 config items from basemodel
13:03:37 DEBUG   opendrift.models.basemodel: Adding 10 config items from basemodel
13:03:37 INFO    opendrift.models.basemodel: OpenDriftSimulation initialised (version 1.7.3 / v1.7.3-17-g291a15b)
13:03:37 DEBUG   opendrift.models.basemodel: Adding 3 config items from openberg
13:03:37 DEBUG   opendrift.models.basemodel:   Overwriting config item seed:wind_drift_factor
13:03:37 DEBUG   opendrift.models.basemodel:   Overwriting config item seed:water_line_length
13:03:37 DEBUG   opendrift.models.basemodel:   Overwriting config item seed:keel_depth

Preparing Readers

reader_current = reader_netCDF_CF_generic.Reader(o.test_data_folder() +
   '16Nov2015_NorKyst_z_surface/norkyst800_subset_16Nov2015.nc')

reader_wind = reader_netCDF_CF_generic.Reader(o.test_data_folder() +
   '16Nov2015_NorKyst_z_surface/arome_subset_16Nov2015.nc')

o.add_reader([reader_current, reader_wind])

Out:

13:03:37 DEBUG   opendrift.models.basemodel: Added reader /root/project/tests/test_data/16Nov2015_NorKyst_z_surface/arome_subset_16Nov2015.nc

Seeding elements

Icebergs are moved with the ocean current as per Barker et al (2004), in addition to a fraction of the wind speed (wind_drift_factor). This factor depends on the properties of the elements. Default empirical values are: - Wind drift fraction: 0.018 (1.8 %) (Garret 1985) - Iceberg size: Keel dept = 60m

Waterline length = 90.5m

o.seed_elements(3.3, 60., radius=3000,
                time=reader_current.start_time,
                water_line_length=100,
                keel_depth=90, number=500)


print('Starting free run .../n')

print('Start time: ' + str(o.start_time))

Out:

Starting free run .../n
Start time: 2015-11-16 00:00:00

Running model

o.run(time_step=3600, steps=steps)
